Line 112 WCAG 2.2 AA F78 Section 508 (2017) AA F78
This link is broken. The target anchor does not exist or is commented out.
id=sign-up
The anchor after the # symbol points to a non-existent id on the target page. If the anchor link targets the same page nothing will happen when it's clicked. If the anchor link targets another page, then the top of the target page will be displayed instead of the intended location. In most cases the destination anchor has been removed accidentally and should be reinstated.

1153<h4 class="h4">

1154A national tasting event celebrating your local restaurant community.</h4>

1155<p class="p">

1156</p>

1157<p class="p light">

1158The James Beard Foundation’s Taste America® presented by Capital One brings together chefs, special guests, and diners from across the country to celebrate the local independent restaurants at the heart of our communities.</p>

1159<p class="p light">

1160The walk-around tasting at The Grand Belle at The Bellevue, in partnership with Cescaphe, will be an exciting gathering of chefs from the Philadelphia culinary community, with food stations hosted by TasteTwenty chef <strong class="strong">

1161Randy Rucker</strong>

1162 of <strong class="strong">

1163River Twice</strong>

1164 and <strong class="strong">

Line 1493 WCAG 2.2 A 4.1.2 Section 508 (2017) A 4.1.2
This button element is empty and has no accessible name.

A programmatically determined name allows screen readers to tell users what the control does. To add a name do one of the following:

  • Add text between the button start and end tags
  • Add a title attribute
  • Add an aria-label attribute
  • Add an aria-labelledby attribute
  • Add an img alt attribute if the button contains an img element
img elements with role=presentation or role=none are not included in the button's accessible name.

1512</button>

The aria-labelledby attribute references a blank element.
Make sure aria-labelledby references an element containing text.
Line 1513 WCAG 2.2 A 4.1.2 Section 508 (2017) A 4.1.2
This button element is empty and has no accessible name.

A programmatically determined name allows screen readers to tell users what the control does. To add a name do one of the following:

  • Add text between the button start and end tags
  • Add a title attribute
  • Add an aria-label attribute
  • Add an aria-labelledby attribute
  • Add an img alt attribute if the button contains an img element
img elements with role=presentation or role=none are not included in the button's accessible name.
Line 1513 WCAG 2.2 A 4.1.2 Section 508 (2017) A 4.1.2
The CSS outline or border style on this element makes it difficult or impossible to see the link focus outline.
:focus and :not(:focus) have same outline:
Do not remove the default outline style, and change any border styles to avoid obscuring the focus outline around focusable elements. See :focus-visible for more information.

Using a border or outline style that obscures the focus ring causes problems for keyboard-only users in:

  • Chrome (obscures the focus indicator on links, buttons, dropdowns and range controls)
  • Firefox (obscures the focus indicator on links)

Line 1548 WCAG 2.2 A 4.1.2 Section 508 (2017) A 4.1.2
This button element is empty and has no accessible name.

A programmatically determined name allows screen readers to tell users what the control does. To add a name do one of the following:

  • Add text between the button start and end tags
  • Add a title attribute
  • Add an aria-label attribute
  • Add an aria-labelledby attribute
  • Add an img alt attribute if the button contains an img element
img elements with role=presentation or role=none are not included in the button's accessible name.
Line 1548 WCAG 2.2 A 4.1.2 Section 508 (2017) A 4.1.2

Using a border or outline style that obscures the focus ring causes problems for keyboard-only users in:

  • Chrome (obscures the focus indicator on links, buttons, dropdowns and range controls)
  • Firefox (obscures the focus indicator on links)

Line 1640 HTML5 ARIA 1.2

1640<div class="FooterPartners_partner__tkir8" aria-label=" ">

img elements must have an accessible name.
Add an alt attribute describing the image, which screen readers voice instead of the image. Spacer images and purely decorative images should use alt="" without any global ARIA attributes. Do not use alt text containing only spaces since that's voiced as an unlabeled image.

Impact on users:

  • NVDA 2023.3 Chrome 120 Windows 10 Reading: Image ignored.
  • NVDA 2023.3 FF 115 Windows 10 Reading: Image ignored.
  • NVDA 2023.3 Edge 120 Windows 10 Reading: Image ignored.
  • JAWS 2023.2311.34 Chrome 120 Windows 10 Reading: Image ignored.
  • JAWS 2023.2311.34 FF 115 Windows 10 Reading: Image ignored.
  • JAWS 2023.2311.34 Edge 120 Windows 10 Reading: Image ignored.
  • VoiceOver macOS 13.6 Safari 16.6 macOS 13.6.0 Reading: Image filename read out.
  • VoiceOver iOS 16.6 Safari iOS 16.6 iOS 16.6.1 Touch: Image filename read out, along with OCR text from image.
Line 1641 WCAG 2.2 A F65 Section 508 (2017) A F65
